## Section 001: Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names the theme without its core principle, dispatch one agent per independent problem domain and let them work concurrently, with independence as the gating test
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's overview states that sequential investigation of unrelated failures wastes time exactly because each investigation is independent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the doctrine collapses when failures are related, when shared state couples the agents, or when exploratory debugging means nobody knows what is broken yet
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference operationalizes the dispatching-parallel-agents skill and does not cover orchestration frameworks beyond its prompt-level pattern
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the one-agent-per-domain principle, the independence test that gates it, and the four-step pattern from domain identification to integration
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the skill treats parallelism as a property of the problem, not the tooling, the decision graph asks about independence and shared state before any dispatch mechanics appear
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to group failures by what is broken, verify domains are independent, dispatch one focused self-contained agent per domain, then review, conflict-check, and run the full suite
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the skill's overview states that sequential investigation of unrelated failures wastes time exactly because each investigation is independent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the doctrine collapses when failures are related, when shared state couples the agents, or when exploratory debugging means nobody knows what is broken yet
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference operationalizes the dispatching-parallel-agents skill and does not cover orchestration frameworks beyond its prompt-level pattern
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: open with the one-agent-per-domain principle, the independence test that gates it, and the four-step pattern from domain identification to integration
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the skill treats parallelism as a property of the problem, not the tooling, the decision graph asks about independence and shared state before any dispatch mechanics appear
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where the doctrine collapses when failures are related, when shared state couples the agents, or when exploratory debugging means nobody knows what is broken yet

- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in two or more tasks exist that can be worked without shared state or sequential dependencies

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: the doctrine collapses when failures are related, when shared state couples the agents, or when exploratory debugging means nobody knows what is broken yet

- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Parallel Agent Dispatch Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: a single agent investigating all failures when they are related, or sequential agents when work is independent but state is shared

## Section 003: Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed scoreboard scores corpus hygiene while the skill's own load-bearing rules go unranked, the independence test, one agent per domain, focused self-contained prompts, and mandatory post-return verification
- **supporting_reason:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill sequences these as gates, independence decides whether to dispatch, prompt discipline decides whether dispatch succeeds, and verification decides whether the results integrate
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the seed's numeric scores were never measured and the skill offers no internal ranking beyond its gate order
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the scoreboard ranks dispatch-discipline rules for adoption priority and does not rank agent platforms
- **revision_decision:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to promote a top tier of four rules, test independence before dispatching, scope one agent per problem domain, give each agent focused self-contained prompts with specified output, and verify with conflict checks plus a full-suite run

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gate names the corpus verifier while the theme's real gates are the skill's post-return sequence, review each summary, check for conflicts, run the full suite, and spot check for systematic errors
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill makes integration conditional on these steps because agents can make systematic errors and independent fixes can still collide
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the gates assume a runnable full suite, dispatches in codebases without one lose their strongest objective check
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the gate set defines what must pass before dispatched results are integrated and does not gate the dispatch decision itself, which the decision graph owns
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to adopt the four-step return gate verbatim, summaries read, conflicts checked, full suite green, and spot checks done, with integration blocked until all four pass
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the gates distrust success reports, an agent returning fixed is treated as a claim to verify, not a result to merge, which is the same stance the corpus takes toward its own references

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's description names its trigger exactly, use when facing 2+ independent tasks that can be worked without shared state or sequential dependencies
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: keying to every mention of parallelism would drag the doctrine into tool-call parallelism and CI concurrency it does not govern
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide routes readers into this reference and does not decompose their problems for them

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's own branches encode the trade, independent and stateless goes parallel, independent but state-sharing goes sequential, related goes single-agent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: independence judgments are fallible, failures that look disjoint can share a hidden root cause discovered only mid-investigation
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide calibrates dispatch aggressiveness per batch and cannot waive the post-return verification gates
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rekey adopt to parallel dispatch for legible independent stateless batches, adapt to sequential agents or narrowed scopes when state couples the work, and avoid for related failures and exploratory debugging

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets classify verification failures generically and never carry this theme's retry rule, a failed dispatch is re-decomposed or re-prompted, never blindly relaunched
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's failure causes are structural, wrong decomposition or defective prompts, and relaunching without changing either reproduces the failure at full parallel cost
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: re-decomposition assumes the coupling is now understood, a second wrong split wastes a second batch
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this governs retrying dispatch batches and reference-verification work, kept as two labeled layers
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the dispatch-layer rules, conflicted integrations get re-decomposition with the coupling folded in, unusable summaries get re-prompting with the missing property added, and coupling discoveries collapse the batch to a single investigator
